< review>
In early August 2019. I been coming here for years. I've learned from police that this area is a extremely hot area for crime, gangs/guns. At times armed individuals come in to hang out at the laundry facility. Calls to police for help. Police won't show up due to concerns over the officers personal safety. 7 Eleven's owner gets police help when called. Homeless love hanging out here. The laundry facility is open 5AM- 10PM. Customer safety is 8AM-12NOON. This is when it's probably safe to do laundry. There needs to be armed security guards here, which will never be. All information was communicated to myself about this area.</review>

< Review>
We had a great experience with this company. We paid $72 for two 24 hour bike rentals and added the $8 insurance just in case. We returned the bicycles the next day but mistakenly forgot the helmets at our apartment. The staff here at Bike and View allowed us to come back the next day and return our helmets no issues. I posted a picture of the rules they have for biking. The location was also very convenient considering you're so close to the Marina. But, with that being said, when you arrive back from Sausalito ferry, you're far away, which makes for a difficult ride to return the bikes.</Review>

< user_name>
Ahmad Amine<//user_name>
< date>
1531086356709<//date>
<Rating>1</Rating>< review>
My worst experience so far in San Francisco. No wonder the bikes are 30% off if you book online: their quality sucks.
To start it off, the bike was noisy from the very beginning as it creaked frequently, especially when changing gears.
Later on in my ride around the coast, the chain slid off the gears when i put the bike in first gear. I was shook and scared but luckily it sorted itself out when i moved it a little.
The gear changes were oh so terrible. Every time i changed gears the transition is sudden that it could take someone less experienced off balance.
The worst part is when i was going up to legion's honor (anyone who has been there knows that its very steep) and logically i had to put the bike in the lowest gear possible. And just so I did. And just so did the chain slip again, this time for good. I had to hike the whole climb up to legion of honor then walk the bike down all the way to get myself a bus back to the trans-bay terminal to return to Berkeley.
I had to haul the broken bike with me between buses till i was back home because the shop closes at 7 and i was way out by 6:30 when this happened.
Luckily i had paid a 4$ insurance that covered the broken parts of the repairs (didn't cover the price of the buses i had to take and the struggle of hauling the bike around).
I did lose the helmet in all the confusion however. THIS was my fault and i expected to pay for it 10-20$.
This brings us to the worst part of the whole experience: the customer service. When i delivered the bike i complained to the lady there that the experience was bad because the chain slipped and i had to carry it around. The lady simply didn't care. All she cared for was the missing helmet to which she charged me 25$. She even had the audacity to tell me that they usually cost them 45$ as if trying to make me feel bad for paying 25$! It's also weird that some people compliment the service. For me, the service was very bland and I didn't receive a map of the area like some people said they got or like most other bike rentals.
The place closes at 7 and you need to get the bike before 6:45 so expect to keep the bike if you wish to explore enough of the bay (i was still exploring fort point by 5 when i took the bike at 2).
TL:DR: Unacceptable bike quality and bad customer service. Don't be lured by the 30% off discount, it's there for a reason. Pay a few bucks extra and rent from more reliable bike rentals.</review>

< Text>
Nice little shop with a friendly staff.  My family rented Bikes to go across the Golden.  Crazy but fantastic day.   My 3 stars only has to do with location and no night drop off.   The location is fine unless you go to Sausalito and ride Ferry back.  It is is closest rental place I could find to the bridge but that means when you come back on Ferry will be furthest to return your bike. Just a preference but after a long tiring day I would rather get off Ferry and not ride several miles.  This may not matter to some but I would have rather rented closer to Ferry and had a longer ride on front end and shorter on back.

Real reason I give 3 stars is they close at 7 PM and have no night drop off.  (other places have night drop offs. )There may be times of year this is no problem but the Ferry wait in Sausalito was close to 2 hrs. (no fault of bike shop) Most places you read about this say be an hour early to Ferry line but it took us much longer.  Ended up landing at the Ferry Building with a 4 mile Bike Ride back to the Bike Shop.  We had about 25 minutes to ride the traffic gauntlet (family of 5).  We barely made it but it was an insane sprint for my kids especially.  A night drop would have solved all.  This is entirely subjective and depends on your needs.  Location closer to Ferry I would give them 3 1/2 stars.  Night drop off for the bikes and I would give them 4 1/2.< /Text>

< review>
This place was literally 10 mins walk from our hotel. Renting was pretty easy - we booked online and then showed up next morning around 10am. They made us sign some waivers - gave us the maps of suggested places to stop at on our way to Sausalito and off we went ! It was mostly downhill or flat from the shop and we stopped at almost all the points on the map (Wave Organ being my personal favorite!). Getting on to the bridge is the only steep uphill and the bikes were actually able to gear-shift through the ride, powered by my burning knees ofcourse. Downhill to Sausalito past  Golden Gate Vista point was the most fun and highly recommended. Once in Sausalito, we parked our bikes at the ferry terminal, purchased our return tickets, grabbed food and beer at Joinery and then hopped back on the ferry to SF. All in all an amazing experience to bike the bridge - highly recommended!<//review>

<review>We came across this place and decided to give it a try while waiting for an order from myhotpot next door. It's a nice cozy place, they only had like 2 tables out now because of the pandemic. The staff was useful and explained everything carefully when we asked. The ordering process is pretty simple, you choose a waffle flavor (original or chocolate), an ice cream flavor (I got rocket pop, which is like a berry sherbet, my friend got cookie monster, they were both really good). Then they go in the back and make them, when they're ready they'll call you in to add additional toppings  (mochi, oreo, marshmallows, m&m, pocky, fruity pebbles, sprinkles, etc.). The waffle was huge, I got full from it and had to walk it off before having my real dinner lol. Small tip: when you get to the middle of the waffle, tear along the line on the wrapper, make your life easier üòÜ< /review><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNgGGeLOsdgxNVyM_a-sbiBtyouLjFZ01RUwtx-=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMZbrExIvYQKuAaAl_IKArjkZ31_u44eVY2uhYD=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//pics>< response>

< Text>
Warm fresh waffle, Delicious Ice Cream, and great/quick  customer service. I get the chocolate waffle because it legitimately tastes like warm, soft Cocoa Puff cereal! Their soft serve is perfect; it's smooth, not too sweet and the flavors are always delicious. They change out flavors every season to give plenty of variety though of the seasonal flavors matcha is definitely my favorite. I also love the unlimited toppings option so you can really go crazy.

The staff is always super friendly and patient and really are just the nicest folks.< /Text>

<user_name>Brian Sim< /user_name><Resp>None< /Resp><Gmap_id>0x80c2b0abe602b21f:0x2a60a305bc422a79< /Gmap_id><date>1553363069710</date><text>This is a long overdue review from our experience in October 2018.

TL;DR: We negotiated a price and signed off an offer sheet. While reviewing the financing agreement, right before signing the final docs, we found that the price on the contract was nearly $3,000 higher than what we agreed to. Nobody informed us of this bait and switch. They were hoping we'd miss the details and sign off at the higher price. When we confronted them about it, they took no responsibility, and scurried to take the deal off the table. The finance guy blamed the sales guy. The sales guy said it was up to the finance guy and the owner. We walked out without the car.

Suggestions:
1. If you're negotiating a deal, take a picture of every offer sheet you see. The numbers will change inexplicably along the way.
2. Don't buy the extended warranty. Or if you really want to, decline multiple times, because they will lower the price by and increase the length and miles covered by 3-4x. It's crazy how much they move on this.
3. Go somewhere else and find a more reputable dealership.

Backstory:
We visited the Nissani Bros Nissan dealership four times over a span of a month in Sep/Oct. Our main sales contacts were Andrew and Flavio. Andrew and Flavio were great. Friendly, pretty helpful, and a pleasure to deal with.

Once we got down to negotiating the price, a guy named Reza, who's the desk guy/former closer, entered the picture. Reza manipulates the price and moves random costs from line item to line item, and has absolutely no credibility.

Eventually, we went back to dealing with Flavio, and that part of the negotiation was much more productive. We settled on a price of around $23K, they showed us an offer sheet and asked my financee to sign her name off on it. We did.

We then wait another hour or so for finance to handle the paperwork for financing. Eventually we meet Damian, the finance guy. Damian seems like a nice guy. He was very persistent in upselling us on an extended warranty policy. He lowered the price of the warranty multiple times, going from about $50/mo down to about $12/mo. At the same time, he kept increasing the length and coverage of the warranty from 4 years and 48,000 miles to 8 years and 125,000 miles. He seems like he's being chummy, but he's not. It's all a blatant cash grab. And at a certain point it just starts feeling desperate.

After about 30 minutes, and declining the extended warranty several times, we got to the point where we were just about to sign the approval on the price and financing, when instead of the $23K price we expected to see, we see it's $26K. We see some costs have changed line items, and  there are brand new costs too. We confront Damian about this price bait and switch. He has no answers. He blamed Reza. We went over to Reza and asked him. He claimed ignorance and said that's determined by finance and the owners.

It was clear to us that they never intended to honor the $23K price we agreed to. It was also clear to us that they were hoping that we'd either not pay enough attention to details and would accidentally sign off on the $26K price without realizing it, or decide that we were too far down the process to walk out on the deal because of the $3K price increase.</text><UserId.>108197464080339240497</UserId.></record></dataset><record>
